## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (ODE growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is the time-derivative of population size P, indicating an ordinary differential equation model for population growth. Typical relationships include per-capita growth depending on density (P) and sometimes explicit time dependence (t) via seasonality, harvesting, or changing environment.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Linear growth/decline: dP_dt = c0 + c1 * P (immigration/emigration plus proportional growth/decay)
- Logistic ODE (Verhulst): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density dependence via carrying capacity)
- Quadratic crowding (equivalent expansion of logistic): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (births ~ P, deaths ~ P^2 from competition)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (nonlinear density dependence strength/shape)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (per-capita growth declines ~ log(P))
- Richards generalized logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2)**c3 (flexible sigmoidal approach to capacity)
- Allee effect (strong) with carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 * P - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below an Allee threshold, negative near capacity)
- Allee effect (weak) rational form: dP_dt = c0 * P * ((c1 * P - 1) / (1 + c2 * P)) (reduced growth at low P with saturation at high P)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed removal rate, e.g., quota harvest)
- Proportional harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (removal proportional to stock size)
- Seasonal forcing of growth rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P (time-varying per-capita growth due to seasons)
- Seasonal forced logistic: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (seasonality plus density dependence)
- Time-varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * exp(c3 * t))) (changing environment/resources over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate view: if dP_dt is proportional to P, model structures often factor as dP_dt = P * g(t, P); checking dP_dt / P vs P helps distinguish mechanisms.
- Density dependence via competition: appearance of a negative P**2 term (or higher powers) indicates crowding/competition where mortality or reduced fecundity increases with density.
- Carrying capacity behavior: factors like (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**theta) encode a stable equilibrium at P ≈ 1/c (or similar), suggesting resource limitation.
- Gompertz-like regulation: log(c/P) in dP_dt typically implies per-capita growth decreases approximately linearly with log(P), common in tumor/ecology size-regulation contexts.
- Allee threshold signature: inclusion of (c*P - 1) (or similar) creates an unstable equilibrium at low P, capturing mate-finding/cooperation limitations and bistability.
- Harvesting/removal processes: additive negative terms (-(constant) or -c*P) represent external mortality/harvest; these can shift equilibria or cause extinction thresholds.
- Seasonality/time forcing: sinusoidal dependence on t in the per-capita rate (e.g., c0 + c1*sin(c2*t)) indicates periodic environmental drivers; look for oscillatory residuals vs t.
- Changing environment/capacity: explicit t inside a capacity-like term (e.g., K(t) in 1 - P/K(t)) reflects habitat/resource change; can produce non-stationary equilibria.
- Near-equilibrium linearization: around a stable equilibrium P*, dP_dt often behaves like -c*(P - P*), so locally linear slopes in dP_dt vs P suggest stability strength.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG18)
============================================================
GT: c0*P*sin(c1*t) + c2*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P
Candidate formulas: 70

Let’s first rewrite the Ground Truth (GT) into a simplified fixed form.

### Ground Truth simplification
GT:
\[
0.4770530111687279\,P\sin(0.7760602430275763\,t)\;+\;0.44545499474048156(1-\tfrac{P}{51.06128580599878})P\;+\;0.44545499474048156P
\]

Expand the quadratic part:
\[
0.44545499474048156(1-\tfrac{P}{51.06128580599878})P
=0.44545499474048156P-\frac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}P^2
\]

So GT is exactly:
\[
\underbrace{\Big(-\frac{0.44545499474048156}{51.06128580599878}\Big)}_{A}P^2
\;+\;\underbrace{(0.44545499474048156+0.44545499474048156)}_{B}P
\;+\;\underbrace{0.4770530111687279}_{C}P\sin(\underbrace{0.7760602430275763}_{\omega}t)
\]
i.e.
\[
A P^2 + B P + C\,P\sin(\omega t)
\]
with **no constant term**, and **no other dependence on \(t\)** except inside the sine.

Compute key fixed coefficients:
- \(A=-0.44545499474048156/51.06128580599878\) (a fixed negative number)
- \(B=0.8909099894809631\)
- \(C=0.4770530111687279\)
- \(\omega=0.7760602430275763\)

So any matching candidate must be reducible (by parameter choices) to:
\[
(\text{const})P^2 + (\text{const})P + (\text{const})P\sin((\text{const})t)
\]
with **no extra terms** (no extra \(t\)-only terms, no logs/exp, no extra trig terms, no phase shift unless removable, etc.).

---

## Candidate-by-candidate analysis

### 1. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4) + Pc5 + c6\,t\,(P+c7)^{c8}\)
To match GT, the last term must vanish for all \(P,t\): set \(c6=0\).
Then we have \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c5) + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4)\), which can match GT by choosing:
- \(c0=A\)
- \(c1+c5=B\)
- \(c2=C\)
- Need \(\sin(c3 t + c4)=\sin(\omega t)\) for all \(t\). This requires \(c3=\omega\) and \(c4=0\) (or \(c4=2k\pi\)).
So **candidate 1 can match**.

### 2. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4) + Pc5(c6+t)^{c7} + Pc8\)
The term \(Pc5(c6+t)^{c7}\) must not introduce nontrivial \(t\)-dependence. Options:
- Set \(c5=0\) to remove it.
Then expression becomes \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c8) + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4)\), which can match as in (1).
So **candidate 2 can match**.

### 3. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4) + Pc5 + P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\log(c9|P|+1)\)
The last term is highly non-polynomial in \(P\) and involves \(\log\). To match GT it must be identically 0: set \(c7=0\).
Then reduces to candidate 8 form \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot)+Pc5\), which can match (see 8).
So **candidate 3 can match**.

### 4. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2\sin(c3 + c4 t) + Pc5 + Pc6\)
Combine: \(P^2(c0+c1)+P(c5+c6)+Pc2\sin(c4 t + c3)\). This matches GT if:
- \(c0+c1=A\)
- \(c5+c6=B\)
- \(c2=C\)
- \(c4=\omega\), \(c3=0\) (mod \(2\pi\))
So **candidate 4 can match**.

### 5. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3\cos(c4 t + c5)\)
Trig is cosine, but cosine can represent sine via phase shift: \(\sin(\omega t)=\cos(\omega t-\pi/2)\).
However the trig term here is **not multiplied by \(P\)**? Actually it is \(P*c3*cos(...)\), yes multiplied by \(P\). Good.
We need linear term \(BP\): provided by \(Pc2\).
Quadratic: \(P^2(c0+c1)\).
So choose:
- \(c0+c1=A\)
- \(c2=B\)
- \(c3=C\)
- \(c4=\omega\)
- \(c5=-\pi/2\) (or equivalent)
So **candidate 5 can match**.

### 6. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3\sin(c4 + c5 t) + Pc6 + Pc7 + Pc8\)
This is \(P^2(c0+c1+c2)+P(c6+c7+c8)+Pc3\sin(c5 t + c4)\). Match by:
- \(c0+c1+c2=A\)
- \(c6+c7+c8=B\)
- \(c3=C\)
- \(c5=\omega\), \(c4=0\) mod \(2\pi\)
So **candidate 6 can match**.

### 7. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + Pc4 + P\)
Linear term is \(P(c4+1)\). Match by:
- \(c0=A\)
- \(c4+1=B\Rightarrow c4=B-1\)
- \(c1=C\)
- \(c2=\omega\), \(c3=0\) mod \(2\pi\)
So **candidate 7 can match**.

### 8. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4) + Pc5\)
This is exactly the needed structure: \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c5) + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4)\).
Choose:
- \(c0=A\)
- \(c1+c5=B\)
- \(c2=C\)
- \(c3=\omega\), \(c4=0\) mod \(2\pi\)
So **candidate 8 can match**.

### 9. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4)\)
Missing an extra free \(P\) coefficient? No: \(Pc1\) already provides the full linear coefficient. So set:
- \(c0=A\)
- \(c1=B\)
- \(c2=C\)
- \(c3=\omega\), \(c4=0\) mod \(2\pi\)
So **candidate 9 can match**.

### 10. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + Pc4\sin(c5 t + c6) + Pc7\)
Linear term is \(P(c2+c3+c7)\), trig term \(P c4 \sin(\cdot)\), quadratic \(P^2(c0+c1)\). Match by choosing sums appropriately and \(c5=\omega, c6=0\).
So **candidate 10 can match**.

### 11. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\cos(c3 t + c4)\)
Cosine can represent sine via phase shift. Choose:
- \(c0=A\)
- \(c1=B\)
- \(c2=C\)
- \(c3=\omega\)
- \(c4=-\pi/2\)
So **candidate 11 can match**.

### 12. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4) + Pc5 + Pc6\)
Linear term \(P(c1+c5+c6)\). Match similarly. **Can match**.

### 13. \(P^2c0/(c1 + c2 e^{c3 t}) + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(c6 t + c7) + Pc8\)
The first term depends on \(t\) unless removed. To match GT (which has no such \(t\)-dependence in the quadratic coefficient), must set \(c0=0\). Then we get \(P(c4+c8)+Pc5\sin(c6 t + c7)\), but GT needs a nonzero \(P^2\) term \(A P^2\). Impossible if \(c0=0\). If \(c0\neq 0\), quadratic coefficient varies with \(t\), impossible. So **cannot match**.

### 14. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(c2 t + c3) + P^{c4}c5\)
To get a \(P^2\) term, set \(c4=2\) so last term is \(c5 P^2\). Then match:
- \(c5=A\)
- \(c0=B\)
- \(c1=C\), \(c2=\omega\), \(c3=0\)
So **candidate 14 can match**.

### 15. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3\cos(c4 t + c5)\)
This is \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c2) + P c3\cos(\cdot)\). Use phase shift for sine. **Can match**.

### 16. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t + c4) + Pc5 + c6\log(c7 e^{Pc8}+1)\)
The log term depends on \(P\) non-polynomially unless removed: set \(c6=0\). Then reduces to candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 17. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5/(c6 t + c7) + Pc8 + c9/(c6 t + c7)\)
To avoid rational-in-\(t\) terms, need \(c5=0\) and \(c9=0\) (or \(c6=0\) but then becomes constants in \(t\); still problematic unless also zero). Setting \(c5=c9=0\) yields \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c8)+Pc2\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 18. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\log(c7 t + 1)\)
The log term depends on \(t\) but GT has no additive \(t\)-only term. Must set \(c6=0\). Then reduces to candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 19. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + P^{c3}c4\cos(\cdot) + c7 e^{c8 t}\)
The \(c7 e^{c8 t}\) term must be zero: set \(c7=0\). Then need trig term to be \(P\sin\), so set \(c3=1\) and phase shift cosine to sine. Then match coefficients. **Can match**.

### 20. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Must set \(c6=0\). Need trig term to be \(P\sin\): set \(c2=1\), phase shift. Then match \(P^2\) and \(P\). **Can match**.

### 21. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 t^{c7}\)
Extra \(t^{c7}\) term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 22. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 t + c7\)
Need no standalone \(t\) or constant term: set \(c6=0\) and \(c7=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 23. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 t/(Pc7+c8) + c9/(Pc7+c8)\)
The rational-in-\(P\) terms must vanish: set \(c6=0\) and \(c9=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 24. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Extra exponential term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 25. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3\cos(\cdot) + c6 + c7 e^{c8 t}\)
Need no constant and no exponential: set \(c6=0\), \(c7=0\). Then need trig term \(P\sin\): set \(c2=1\) and phase shift. **Can match**.

### 26. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4/(c5+t)^5 + Pc6(1-(Pc7)^{c8})^{c9}\)
Hard extra nonlinear \(P\) term and rational-in-\(t\) term. To remove: set \(c4=0\) and \(c6=0\). Then left with \(P(c0 + c1\sin(\cdot))\), but GT needs a \(P^2\) term. Impossible. **Cannot match**.

### 27. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5/(c6+t)^5 + Pc7\)
Remove rational-in-\(t\): set \(c5=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c7)+Pc2\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 28. \(P^2c0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4 + c5\)
GT has no constant term: set \(c5=0\). Then match \(P^2\), \(P\), and sine term. **Can match**.

### 29. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\cos(\cdot) + c5\)
Set \(c5=0\), phase shift cosine to sine, match coefficients. **Can match**.

### 30. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6(Pc7)^{c8} + c6\)
To remove constant \(+c6\), must set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 31. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\)
Need no constant: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 32. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + Pc6 + c7\)
Need no constant: set \(c7=0\). Linear term becomes \(P(c1+c5+c6)\). **Can match**.

### 33. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3+c4 t) + Pc5/(c6+t)^5\)
Remove rational-in-\(t\): set \(c5=0\). Then match sine with \(c4=\omega, c3=0\). **Can match**.

### 34. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2\sin(c3+c4 t) + Pc5 + Pc6 + Pc7/(c8+t)^5\)
Remove rational-in-\(t\): set \(c7=0\). Then match sums for \(P^2\) and \(P\), and sine args. **Can match**.

### 35. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 t/(c7 t + c8) + c9/(c7 t + c8)\)
Extra rational-in-\(t\) terms must vanish: set \(c6=0\), \(c9=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 36. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\sin(Pc7 + c8)\)
The last term depends on \(P\) inside sine; GT has no such dependence. Must set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 37. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4/(c5+t)^5 + P^{c6}c7\)
Remove rational-in-\(t\): set \(c4=0\). To get \(P^2\), set \(c6=2\) so last term is \(c7P^2\). Then match \(c7=A\), \(c0=B\), \(c1=C\), etc. **Can match**.

### 38. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4/(c5+t)^5 + P^{c6}c7 e^{c8 t}\)
If \(c7\neq 0\), the \(P^{c6}e^{c8 t}\) term introduces \(t\)-dependence in the polynomial part; GT has none. To remove it set \(c7=0\), but then no \(P^2\) term remains (only \(P\) and sine). Alternatively set \(c8=0\) to remove \(t\)-dependence, then \(P^{c6}c7\) can supply \(P^2\) with \(c6=2\). Also set \(c4=0\). Then it matches. **Can match**.

### 39. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(\cdot) + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
The term \(P^2c1\sin(\cdot)\) is a \(P^2\sin(t)\) interaction not present in GT; cannot be canceled by other terms (no other \(P^2\sin\) term). Only way is \(c1=0\). Also must remove exponential: set \(c6=0\). Then becomes \(P^2c0 + P(c4 + c5\sin(\cdot))\) which can match by setting \(c0=A\), \(c4=B\), \(c5=C\), and sine args. **Can match**.

### 40. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5/(Pc6+c7) + Pc8 + c9/(Pc6+c7)\)
Rational-in-\(P\) terms must vanish: set \(c5=0\), \(c9=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + P(c1+c8)+Pc2\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 41. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4\log(c5/(P+c6)+1) + P^{c7}c8\)
The log term depends on \(P\) non-polynomially; must set \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c7=2\) so \(P^{c7}c8=c8P^2\). Match coefficients and sine args. **Can match**.

### 42. \(Pc0/(P+c1) + Pc2 + Pc3\sin(\cdot) + P^{c6}c7\)
The term \(Pc0/(P+c1)\) is not polynomial in \(P\) unless \(c0=0\). If \(c0=0\), we can set \(c6=2\) to get \(P^2\) and match the rest. **Can match**.

### 43. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\sin(c7 t + c8)\)
Two separate sine-in-\(t\) terms would generally not combine into one unless the second is removed. Set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 44. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\log(Pc7+1)\)
Log term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 45. \(P^2c0 + Pc1/(P+c2) + Pc3 + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(\cdot) + Pc8\)
The \(Pc1/(P+c2)\) term is non-polynomial unless \(c1=0\). Set \(c1=0\). Then we have \(P^2c0 + P(c3+c4+c8) + Pc5\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 46. \(Pc0/(P+c1) + Pc2 + Pc3(Pc4+1)^{c5} + Pc6 + Pc7\sin(\cdot)\)
To avoid non-polynomial terms: set \(c0=0\). Also need no extra nonlinear \( (Pc4+1)^{c5}\) unless it becomes linear/quadratic polynomial. Easiest: set \(c3=0\) to remove it. Then expression is \(P(c2+c6)+Pc7\sin(\cdot)\) with no \(P^2\) term, so cannot match. If instead try to make \(Pc3(Pc4+1)^{c5}\) produce \(P^2\) while not producing higher powers: choose \(c5=1\) gives \(Pc3(Pc4+1)=c3c4 P^2 + c3 P\), which is perfect. Then match:
- \(c3c4 = A\)
- \(c2+c6+c3 = B\)
- \(c7=C\), sine args match.
So **can match**.

### 47. \(P^2c0 + Pc1/(P+c2) + Pc3 + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(\cdot)\)
Set \(c1=0\) to remove rational term. Then \(P^2c0 + P(c3+c4)+Pc5\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 48. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + Pc6\log(c7/(P+c8)+1)\)
Log term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 49. \(P^2c0 + Pc1/(P+c2) + Pc3 + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(\cdot) + c8\)
Need no constant: set \(c8=0\). Also set \(c1=0\) to remove rational term. Then matches as in 47. **Can match**.

### 50. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\exp(c7\sin(\cdot))\)
Exponential-of-sine term must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 51. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4 + Pc5(Pc6)^{c7}\)
Last term is \(P \cdot c5 \cdot (Pc6)^{c7} = c5 c6^{c7} P^{c7+1}\). To get \(P^2\), need \(c7=1\), giving \(c5 c6 P^2\). Then match:
- \(c5 c6 = A\)
- \(c0+c4 = B\)
- \(c1=C\), sine args match.
So **can match**.

### 52. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3 + Pc4\sin(\cdot) + Pc7 + Pc8/(c9+t)^5\)
GT has no \(P^3\): must set \(c0=0\). Remove rational-in-\(t\): set \(c8=0\). Then we have \(P^2(c1+c2)+P(c3+c7)+Pc4\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 53. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + P^{c6}c7\cos(\cdot)\)
Extra trig term must be removed: set \(c7=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 54. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} + Pc6\sin(\cdot) + Pc9\)
The term \(Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} = c3 c4^{c5} P^{c5+1}\). To avoid extra powers beyond \(P^2\), choose \(c5=1\) giving a \(P^2\) contribution. Then match coefficients by distributing between \(P^2c0\) and this term, and linear term from \(Pc1+Pc2+Pc9\). **Can match**.

### 55. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3 + Pc4\sin(\cdot) + Pc7\)
Set \(c0=0\). Then \(P^2(c1+c2)+P(c3+c7)+Pc4\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 56. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + P^2c3 + Pc4 + Pc5 + Pc6\sin(\cdot) + Pc9\)
Set \(c0=0\). Then \(P^2(c1+c2+c3)+P(c4+c5+c9)+Pc6\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 57. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3 + P^{c4}c5\cos(\cdot) + c8 e^{c9 t}\)
Remove \(P^3\): set \(c0=0\). Remove exponential: set \(c8=0\). Need trig term to be \(P\sin\): set \(c4=1\) and phase shift cosine. Then match remaining coefficients. **Can match**.

### 58. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + P^{c4}c5\sin(\cdot)\)
To avoid having two independent sine terms, easiest is set \(c5=0\) leaving no \(P^2\). Alternatively make the second sine identical to the first (same frequency/phase) so they combine: set its sine args equal to the first’s, and choose \(c4=1\) so it’s also \(P\sin\), but then still no \(P^2\). If \(c4=2\), it becomes \(P^2\sin(\cdot)\) which GT does not have. So **cannot match**.

### 59. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + Pc6 + Pc7\sin(\cdot)\)
If the two sine terms share the same argument, they combine. Set \(c8=c3\), \(c9=c4\) (as needed) so both are \(\sin(\omega t)\), then amplitude is \(c2+c7\). Linear term is \(P(c1+c5+c6)\). **Can match**.

### 60. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + P^{c6}c7\)
To avoid extra powers, either set \(c7=0\) (then candidate 8 form) or set \(c6=2\) and absorb into quadratic coefficient (but then you still have both \(P^2c0\) and \(P^2\) from this term—fine). **Can match**.

### 61. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(\cdot) + c6\sin(\cdot)\)
The \(P^2\sin\) term must be removed: set \(c1=0\). The standalone sine term \(c6\sin(\cdot)\) must be removed too (GT has no term independent of \(P\)): set \(c6=0\). Then \(P^2c0 + P(c4 + c5\sin(\cdot))\) matches. **Can match**.

### 62. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6\log(Pc7+1)\sin(\cdot)\)
The last term is \(\log(Pc7+1)\sin(\cdot)\), not present in GT; must set \(c6=0\). Then reduces to \(P^2(c0+c1)+Pc2\sin(\cdot)+Pc5\), which can match by setting \(Pc5\) to be the linear term (and no separate \(Pc1\) but that’s fine). **Can match**.

### 63. \(P^2c0 + P^2c1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4 + Pc5\sin(\cdot) + Pc8 + Pc9\sin(\cdot)\)
Remove \(P^2\sin\): set \(c1=0\). Combine sine terms: \(P(c5+c9)\sin(\cdot)\). Linear term \(P(c4+c8)\). **Can match**.

### 64. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 e^{Pc7}\)
Exponential in \(P\) must vanish: set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 65. \(P^3c0 + P^2c1 + P^2c2 + Pc3/(P+c4) + Pc5 + Pc6 + Pc7\sin(\cdot)\)
Need no \(P^3\): set \(c0=0\). The rational term \(Pc3/(P+c4)\) must be removed: set \(c3=0\). Then \(P^2(c1+c2)+P(c5+c6)+Pc7\sin(\cdot)\). **Can match**.

### 66. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + P^{c6}c7 e^{Pc8}\)
The last term has \(e^{Pc8}\) unless removed. Only way to avoid non-polynomial dependence is set \(c7=0\) (or \(c8=0\) but still leaves \(P^{c6}\) extra power). Setting \(c7=0\) reduces to candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 67. \(P^2c0/(Pc1+c2) + Pc3/(P+c4) + Pc5/(Pc1+c2) + Pc6 + Pc7\sin(\cdot)\)
All the rational-in-\(P\) terms must be removed to match a polynomial in \(P\). If set \(c0=0,c3=0,c5=0\), then no \(P^2\) term remains. If try to make \(P^2c0/(Pc1+c2)\) equal \(A P^2\) for all \(P\), impossible because it behaves like \(P\) for large \(P\) (if \(c1\neq 0\)) or like \(P^2\) times constant only if denominator constant (requires \(c1=0\)), but then it becomes \((c0/c2)P^2\) which is fine. However then \(Pc5/(Pc1+c2)\) with \(c1=0\) becomes \((c5/c2)P\) (fine) and \(Pc3/(P+c4)\) with \(c3\neq 0\) is not linear; must set \(c3=0\). With \(c1=0\), the expression becomes:
\[
(c0/c2)P^2 + (c5/c2)P + Pc6 + Pc7\sin(\cdot)
\]
This *can* match by choosing \(c0/c2=A\), \(c5/c2 + c6 = B\), \(c7=C\). So **candidate 67 can match** (set \(c1=0, c3=0\), and choose \(c2\neq 0\)).

### 68. \(P^2c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(\cdot) + Pc5 + c6 e^{c7 t}\sin(\cdot)\)
The last term is \(e^{c7 t}\sin(\cdot)\) (not multiplied by \(P\)) and cannot appear in GT. Must set \(c6=0\). Then candidate 8 form. **Can match**.

### 69. \(Pc0/(P+c1) + Pc2 + Pc3\sin(\cdot) + Pc6/(Pc7+c8) + c9/(Pc7+c8)\)
All rational-in-\(P\) terms must be removed: set \(c0=0\), \(c6=0\), \(c9=0\). Then left with \(P(c2 + c3\sin(\cdot))\), no \(P^2\) term. Impossible. **Cannot match**.

### 70. \(Pc0 + Pc1\sin(\cdot) + Pc4/(Pc5+c6) + Pc7/(c8+t)^5 + c9/(Pc5+c6)\)
Has rational-in-\(P\) terms and rational-in-\(t\) term. To remove: set \(c4=0\), \(c7=0\), \(c9=0\). Then left with \(P(c0 + c1\sin(\cdot))\), no \(P^2\) term. Impossible. **Cannot match**.

---

Candidates that **cannot** match: **13, 26, 58, 69, 70**.  
Many others **can** match (e.g., 1, 8, 9, …).

+ c6*exp(c7*t)*sin(c8*t + c9)"]

I need to compare each candidate to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.4770530111687279*P*sin(0.7760602430275763*t) + 0.44545499474048156*(1 - P/51.06128580599878)*P + 0.44545499474048156*P`

Let me expand the GT:
- `0.477053*P*sin(0.776060*t)` — P*sin(t) term
- `0.445455*(1 - P/51.0613)*P` = `0.445455*P - 0.445455*P²/51.0613` = `0.445455*P - 0.008724*P²`
- `0.445455*P`

So GT = `-0.008724*P² + 0.89091*P + 0.477053*P*sin(0.776060*t)`

**GT structure:** `a*P² + b*P + c*P*sin(d*t)` where a < 0, b > 0, c > 0, d > 0.

Now I'll check each candidate to see if it can reduce to this form.

**Candidate 1:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5 + c6*t*(P + c7)^c8`
The last term `c6*t*(P+c7)^c8` introduces a `t` dependence that's not purely `P*sin(d*t)`. Setting c6=0 eliminates it, giving `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c5) + P*c2*sin(c3*t+c4)`. With c4=0, this matches GT form. ✓
Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5*(c6 + t)^c7 + P*c8`
The term `P*c5*(c6+t)^c7` — setting c5=0 eliminates it. Then: `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c8) + P*c2*sin(c3*t+c4)`. With c4=0, matches. ✓
Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5 + P^c6*c7*exp(c8*t)*log(c9*|P|+1)`
Setting c7=0 eliminates the last term. Remaining: `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c5) + P*c2*sin(c3*t+c4)`. With c4=0, matches. ✓
Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `P²*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + P*c5 + P*c6`
= `P²*(c0+c1) + P*(c5+c6) + P*c2*sin(c4*t+c3)`. This is `a*P² + b*P + c*P*sin(d*t+e)`. With c3=0, matches GT. ✓
Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `P²*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2 + P*c3*cos(c4*t + c5)`
= `P²*(c0+c1) + P*c2 + P*c3*cos(c4*t+c5)`. Since cos(x+c5) = sin(x+c5+π/2), this can match. ✓
Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** `P²*c0 + P²*c1 + P²*c2 + P*c3*sin(c4 + c5*t) + P*c6 + P*c7 + P*c8`
= `P²*(c0+c1+c2) + P*(c6+c7+c8) + P*c3*sin(c5*t+c4)`. Matches with c4=0. ✓
Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 7:** `P²*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + P*c4 + P`

Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 8:** `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3*t + c4) + P*c5`

cos can become sin with phase shift. Matches. ✓

**Candidate 58:** `P*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + P^c4*c5*sin(c6*t + c7)`
For this to match GT, we need the last term to give P² (constant, not oscillating). Set c5=0: `P*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t+c3)`. Missing P² term. Can't match. Or set c4=2, then `c5*P²*sin(c6*t+c7)` — this is P²*sin, not a constant*P². We'd need sin to be constant, meaning c6=0, then `c5*P²*sin(c7)` = constant*P². So: `P*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t+c3) + const*P²`. Matches! ✓
Candidate 58 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 59:** Set c7=0 (eliminate second sin): `P²*c0 + P*(c1+c5+c6) + P*c2*sin(c3*t+c4)`. Matches. ✓
